    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10986976130422390039">In the deft hands of <strong>Neil Gaiman</strong>, magic is no mere illusion... and anything is possible. In this, Gaiman's first book of short stories, his imagination and supreme artistry transform a mundane world into a place of terrible wonders -- a place where an old woman can purchase the Holy Grail at a thrift store, where assassins advertise their services in the Yellow Pages under</span>
  <span id="freeText10986976130422390039" style="display:none">In the deft hands of <strong>Neil Gaiman</strong>, magic is no mere illusion... and anything is possible. In this, Gaiman's first book of short stories, his imagination and supreme artistry transform a mundane world into a place of terrible wonders -- a place where an old woman can purchase the Holy Grail at a thrift store, where assassins advertise their services in the Yellow Pages under "Pest Control," and where a frightened young boy must barter for his life with a mean-spirited troll living beneath a bridge by the railroad tracks. Explore a new reality -- obscured by smoke and darkness, yet brilliantly tangible -- in this extraordinary collection of short works by a master prestidigitator. It will dazzle your senses, touch your heart, and haunt your dreams.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10986976130422390039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_1358538').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_1358538').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_1358538').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I have to disagree with everyone else here. There is not "lots" of sex, profanity, and violence; there is SOME sex, profanity, and violence. I started<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I have to disagree with everyone else here. There is not "lots" of sex, profanity, and violence; there is SOME sex, profanity, and violence. I started reading Stephen King when I was about 11. It's the parents' call, of course, but this is pretty tame.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_3160292409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3160292409" />
    <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn"><img alt="Kevin Kuhn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508679965p2/59568642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3160292409?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin Kuhn" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn">Kevin Kuhn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59568642-kevin-kuhn?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59568642-kevin-kuhn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3160292409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17670239971866476261">Gaiman is literary bacon - short stories, young adult, fantasy, adult fiction - he’s good in anything! “Smoke and Mirrors” is a collection of 30 or so short stories. They run the gamut from sci-fi to very short parables to fantasy to magical realism. It’s not his best work, but as a collection it’s imaginative and provocative. I enjoyed a majority of these stories and Gaiman continues to be one of my favorite authors. Some of my preferences were “Chivalry”, “Changes”, “We Can Get Them for You Wh</span>
  <span id="freeText17670239971866476261" style="display:none">Gaiman is literary bacon - short stories, young adult, fantasy, adult fiction - he’s good in anything! “Smoke and Mirrors” is a collection of 30 or so short stories. They run the gamut from sci-fi to very short parables to fantasy to magical realism. It’s not his best work, but as a collection it’s imaginative and provocative. I enjoyed a majority of these stories and Gaiman continues to be one of my favorite authors. Some of my preferences were “Chivalry”, “Changes”, “We Can Get Them for You Wholesale”, and “Snow, Glass, Apples”. <br /><br />One of my favored aspects of Gaiman is his ability to slip seamlessly between realism and fantasy. One moment the story feels like an honest recollection of his past, and the next we're interacting with angels, trolls, and werewolves. He so deft with his word choice that these transitions happen with ease. A good example of this is “The Price”, where Gaiman story about stray cats turns from reality to supernatural in an instant. This ability also really stood out to me in a different book - “The Ocean at the End of the Lane”. I can’t help but admire his mind. It’s the little things like referring to crabs and fish as “ . . . filled with things with too many legs and other things with no legs at all.” <br /><br />In this collection, Gaiman is daring, taking on explicit sex, politics, pornography, and even sex change. Of course, this book was originally published in 1998, when navigating these waters were a little less turbulent than today. The book includes an Introduction which gives a short description of the inspiration or background of each story. I found myself flipping back and forth to this section after each story. For example, in the particularly sexually graphic story “Tastings”, Gaiman admits that the story took him four years to write, largely because he was embarrassed by it. I always appreciate short story collections where the author reveals a bit of their motivation, inspiration, or background of the stories.<br /><br />One note on 'Changes', it's a creative story idea about the cure for cancer having the side effect of gender change which society turns into recreational use. It's laid out almost as author notes for a novel. And it could be a fascinating, controversial, and complex novel. But why include it in this form? Why not write it? Weird, and I found it wasteful and disappointing.<br /><br />An aptly titled collection of stories, where Gaiman does indeed use sleight of word and a bit of magic to make the unbelievable feel just about real.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17670239971866476261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2177751188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177751188" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177751188?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177751188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer958190641768368986">I keep saying, "one more Neil Gaiman book and I'll figure out what the big deal is..." Spoiler, I haven't yet. Though, I did enjoy <i>some</i> of these stories (indicated by a *). There's far more that weren't enjoyable.<br/><br/><b>Introduction</b> - PLEASE skip - this is so, so long. It's a short story in and of itself. Though, technically he hid another short story within that: <b>The Wedding Present </b> - Originally written as a wedding present, this marriage slowly but surely sinks to the pits of despair. <br/><br/><b>Chivalry</b> - A c</span>
  <span id="freeText958190641768368986" style="display:none">I keep saying, "one more Neil Gaiman book and I'll figure out what the big deal is..." Spoiler, I haven't yet. Though, I did enjoy <i>some</i> of these stories (indicated by a *). There's far more that weren't enjoyable.<br /><br /><b>Introduction</b> - PLEASE skip - this is so, so long. It's a short story in and of itself. Though, technically he hid another short story within that: <b>The Wedding Present </b> - Originally written as a wedding present, this marriage slowly but surely sinks to the pits of despair. <br /><br /><b>Chivalry</b> - A cute story about an elderly lady snapping up the Holy Grail at a bargain at the thrift shop. Later republished in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47699.M_Is_for_Magic" title="M Is for Magic by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener"> M is for Magic</a>. <br /><br /><b>Nicholas Was...</b> - A 100-word story centered on St Nicholas for one of Gaiman's Christmas cards.<br /><br /><b>The Price*</b> - this cat deserves a medal, a ball of yarn and a tuna fillet for defending this family against the devil. Republished in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47699.M_Is_for_Magic" title="M Is for Magic by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">M Is for Magic</a>.<br /><br /><b> Troll Bridge </b> - Retelling of the three Billy Goats Gruff. While this started on a high note -<br /> undue time is used to describe the troll's flaccid genitalia. Un-ironically, troll acts like a dick. Republished in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47699.M_Is_for_Magic" title="M Is for Magic by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">M Is for Magic</a>.<br /><br /><b>Don't Ask Jack</b> - Menacing Jack-in-the-Box. (As if I needed another reason to <i>never</i> buy one) Republished in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47699.M_Is_for_Magic" title="M Is for Magic by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">M Is for Magic</a>.<br /><br /><b>The Goldfish Pool and Other Stories</b> - Almost written as a reflection for Neil Gaiman on hollywood. I was not a fan of his comments.<br /><br /><b>Eaten (Scenes from a Moving picture)</b> - please, Gaiman, why does everything need to be so sex-explicit?? Excuse me as I scrub my eyes.<br /><br /><b>The White Road*</b> - This wasn't memorable<br /><br /><b>Queen of Knives</b> - well-written by not memorable.<br /><br /><b>The Facts in the Case of the Departure of Miss Finch</b> - The underground circus leads to the disappearing of one Mrs. Finch. I wasn't a fan of the book and wasn't a fan of the short story. It made too many leaps. <br /><br /><b>Changes</b> - Once again, a Gaiman story became weirdly sexual. (I really should start expecting this). A man discovers the cure for cancer (which has the side effect of changing a person's gender). Now the world is populated by nearly immortal pill-popping gender switchers (I hesitate to call everyone trans since this is done so reversibly and recreationaly)<br /><br /><b>The Daughter of Owls</b> - A girl was found with some owls. The locals hate her.<br /><br /><b>Shoggoth's Old Peculiar</b> - H. P. Lovecraft inspired cult-y New England tale. Did like how he portrayed the pub though.<br /> <br /><b>Virus</b> - Honestly wasn't that memorable. <br /><br /><b>Looking for the Girl</b> - A kid looking at a dirty mag spots the most beautiful girl. As an adult, he finds her again in the mag - but she looks exactly the same. Logically, he devotes his life to becoming the best dirty-mag photographer in hopes of meeting this chick in person. My interpretation: A vampire wanted a free photo-shoot every few years and went to a magazine to do it.<br /><br /><b>Only the End of the World Again</b> - Richly worded, not an interesting plot.<br /><br /><b>Bay Wolf</b> - Baywatch + Beowulf. Surprisingly quirky and fun <br /><br /><b>Fifteen Painted Cards from a Vampire Tarot</b> - Each of the Major Arcana (first 22 of the 78 tarot cards in a deck) is interpreted through a short story. <br /><br /><b>We Can Get Them For You Wholesale*</b> - How good would the bargain need to be to end the world? Despite the dark implications - this was a fun read!!<br /><br /><b>One Life, Furnished in Early Moorcock</b> - High school kid who wanted to write and is a huge fan of a series. He mail-orders a book and never pays for it.<br /><br /><b>Cold Colors</b> - Short poem involving magic and computers <br /><br /><b>The Sweeper of Dreams</b> - prose piece...waxes poetic about dreams and their implications<br /><br /><b>Foreign Parts</b> Sudden sexuality again. A man is slowly taken over by a cognizant venereal disease. Copious mentions of STDs and masturbation.<br /><br /><b>Vampire Sestina</b> - A vampire poem<br /><br /><b>Mouse </b>- The married couple's house is infested. The man buys a humane mousetrap while his wife seems to get an abortion. The man seems to have no reaction to the abortion. Upon finding a mouse trapped, he sets the mouse free outside. <br /><br /><b> The Sea Change*</b> Lyrical poem about mermaids and the ocean.<br /><br /><b>How Do You Think It Feels?</b> - Man goes to conference. Man meets hot girl. Man cheats on wife, despite having a couple of kids. He justifies it (kids are stupid, wife is lame). <br /><br /><b>When We Went to See the End of the World by Dawnie Morningside, age 11¼</b> - Written from the perspective of a child as the end of the world occurs. Unexpectedly chilling.<br /><br /><b>Desert Wind</b> - Man gets lost in the desert and is found.<br /><br /><b>Tastings</b> - Male Prostitute + Female Celebrity. Prostitute has "powers" which lead him to be amazing in bed - essentially he reads the minds of his clients without realizing it - and he can't read Celebrity's and thus is sucking (not literally...well, maybe a bit) in bed. The mundane conversation as they try out positions made this one marginally tolerable. Mostly, I was cringing away from the pages.<br /><br /><b>In the End</b> - Genesis creation in reverse. Not particularly memorable.<br /><br /><b>Babycakes</b> - Just take that title literally.<br /><br /><b>Murder Mysteries</b> - The first murder in heaven as it's investigated by the angel Raguel. <br /><br /><b>Snow, Glass, Apples</b> - Finally! <b>
  <i>FINALLY</i>
</b> I thought as I got to this one. It's a retelling of Snow White with a huge reversal. Snow is evil and the stepmother is <i>attempting</i> to hold together the kingdom from the terror of one, very cruel Snow. <b>What ruined it:</b> The weird sex bits. I would've loved this story if A) Young Snow (as in <i>not over 18, more like 12 or younger</i> hadn't blown a traveling monk before killing him AND B) if the prince wasn't into necrophilia when he screwed first the stepmother and then her daughter. It just completely threw the whole story off. Without it, I would've really enjoyed this creepy retelling.<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="958190641768368986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_38777647" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38777647" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1033675-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325271531p2/1033675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38777647?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/1033675-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38777647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10782663121453434775">'Smoke and Mirrors' is the first of two short story collections written by Neil Gaiman. This title was first published in 1998, while 'Fragile Things' came out in 2006. Having read 'Fragile Things' mere months ago I was doing quite a bit of comparison between the two as I worked my way through 'Smoke and Mirrors'. While there are a lot of similarities between the two, there are also many differences.<br/><br/>Both collections involve Gaiman doing what he does best, that is taking our own myths, fables, an</span>
  <span id="freeText10782663121453434775" style="display:none">'Smoke and Mirrors' is the first of two short story collections written by Neil Gaiman. This title was first published in 1998, while 'Fragile Things' came out in 2006. Having read 'Fragile Things' mere months ago I was doing quite a bit of comparison between the two as I worked my way through 'Smoke and Mirrors'. While there are a lot of similarities between the two, there are also many differences.<br /><br />Both collections involve Gaiman doing what he does best, that is taking our own myths, fables, and folklore, tweaking them to better resonate with our modern culture, and handing them back to us complete with the grit and gristle that were absent from the versions that we received as children. While this seems to be an over-arching theme to most of the stories in 'Fragile Things', it still shows up occasionally in 'Smoke and Mirrors' along with so much else. <br /><br />Gaiman takes the reader to so many places throughout these stories. These include a couple of nods to writers that surely influenced him along the way (Lovecraft and Moorcock, specifically), a writer struggling through a screenplay that has been watered down by the movie studio discovering the legendary Hollywood of old, and political intrigue amongst the angels in heaven. Lawrence Talbot also makes an appearance in a tale involving the Wolf Man. Gaiman's books are usually shelved in the Sci-Fi/Fantasy section at the average bookstore, which I think is a bit of a disservice as these stories are so much more diverse than the typical view of the Fantasy genre that involves touchy-feely knights riding around on horses and tends to prejudice the typical reader to that genre negatively.<br /><br />A tip to any readers who are in the habit of skipping book introductions: Gaiman actually hides a story within the introduction of this book as a payoff to those who religiously read the introduction. That sort of cleverness suckers me in every time.<br /><br />It may be unwise to compare the stories in 'Smoke and Mirrors' to each other and to 'Fragile Things' as both books represent more of a compilation of Gaiman stories that appeared in other publications over a particular period of his writing career versus something that was put together as an intentional, unified collection. However, as it is great fun to wildly speculate, I believe that the stories in 'Smoke and Mirrors' are bolder than the ones in the later collection. As most of these stories were written around the time that 'Sandman' was finishing its run, I'm wondering if the reason for this was to prove to any naysayers that Gaiman was a serious writer and not just "that comic book guy."<br /><br />These stories may not be something that would be discussed in a college level literature class with the austere professor that lives and dies by the canon, but I don't think that is Gaiman's intention as a writer. He comes from the storyteller tradition, and I feel that such a thing is just as important in feeding one's imagination and intellect as the heavy literature now and again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10782663121453434775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46868996" />
    <a title="Jc" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1038815-jc"><img alt="Jc" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321228818p2/1038815.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46868996?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer46868996" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13168313917307437457">This collection of short works, some not quite complete, is maybe a must read for real Gaiman fans who read everything he does (4 stars for them), but not really for anyone else (only 1 star for the general audience). And I say that as one of those fans. I really like what Gaiman does, both in traditional and graphic novel form, but Smoke and Mirrors is not representative of his best work. Basically, it is a collection of things he never bothered to give a final polish to. Much of S&M is things </span>
  <span id="freeText13168313917307437457" style="display:none">This collection of short works, some not quite complete, is maybe a must read for real Gaiman fans who read everything he does (4 stars for them), but not really for anyone else (only 1 star for the general audience). And I say that as one of those fans. I really like what Gaiman does, both in traditional and graphic novel form, but Smoke and Mirrors is not representative of his best work. Basically, it is a collection of things he never bothered to give a final polish to. Much of S&amp;M is things that were just workbook exercises, not intended for publication. Some fun ideas, and entertaining for the fan (or for those who want to study how he develops ideas), but others should try American Gods, Anansi Boys, Neverwhere, Good Omens (with T.Pratchett!), or even Coraline or his Sandman graphic novels. It does, however, contain a few real gems for fans. [warning: different editions of the S&amp;M varied the collection slightly, so referring to specific stories may be confusing when discussing the book]</span>

  <span id="freeText15960497135136683288" style="display:none">Initially read in 1999 or thereabouts. Not reviewed at the time.<br /><br />Upon re-reading:<br /><br />***** “The Goldfish Pond and Other Stories” by Neil Gaiman<br />I'm usually not that interested in the whole 'glamour of Hollywood' theme, but this is probably the best commentary on it I've ever read. <br />Clearly partially autobiographical, this tells the story of a British writer who's flown out to L.A. to talk about converting his bestselling novel into a movie.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_376488646" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/376488646" />
    <a title="April" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10478000-april"><img alt="April" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605047392p2/10478000.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/376488646?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April" href="/user/show/10478000-april">April</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Gaiman fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=short-story-or-stories">short-story-or-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=loved">loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer376488646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13587725593892175782"><i> Bearing in mind I read this on my kindle, so some stories weren't included in the version I read. Also this is hella long.</i><br/><br/><i>All ratings (including notes). * indicates favourite</i><br/><b>The Wedding Present (Yes, I religiously read introductions):4*</b><br/>In which a picturesque couple are given a quaint wedding present that seems to be a 'retelling' of their coupling; it spins a story of how their marriage could have went wrong. Though this premise may seem outlandish and bizarre, it's terribly relevant and poses </span>
  <span id="freeText13587725593892175782" style="display:none"><i> Bearing in mind I read this on my kindle, so some stories weren't included in the version I read. Also this is hella long.</i><br><br><i>All ratings (including notes). * indicates favourite</i><br><b>The Wedding Present (Yes, I religiously read introductions):4*</b><br>In which a picturesque couple are given a quaint wedding present that seems to be a 'retelling' of their coupling; it spins a story of how their marriage could have went wrong. Though this premise may seem outlandish and bizarre, it's terribly relevant and poses significant questions about the lives we choose to live. It's sad to think that some Gaiman fans miss this story;it's precious. <br><b>Chivalry:</b>3.5<br>Quite lovely. The relationship was sweet and Mrs. Whitaker was charming to read. <br><b>Nicholas Was...:</b>4.5<br>An excellent and precisely one hundred word twist on St. Nicholas, aka Santa Claus. Ho ho ho.<br><b>The Price:</b>4<br>Ooh symbolism, symbolism! I adore this story, possibly because I'm so fond of cats. The idea of a knightly cat guardian is wonderful. <br><b>Troll Bridge:</b>3.5<br>I enjoyed this tale, but something lead me to believe that it would be more than it was when it finished, so I wasn't as impressed with the ending. Nevertheless it was immensely thought-provoking and preoccupying. <br><b>Don't Ask Jack:</b>5*<br>Horrifying, afflicting, and downright disturbing. Yep, one of my favourite stories out of the entire book. <br><b>The Goldfish Pool and Other Stories:</b>3<br>I really liked the vintage Hollywood theme but it didn't pull me in. I think I maintained interest simply because it's a quasi-account of personal experience for Gaiman (as he admitted at the start of the book). Riddled with idioms and scathing remarks on Hollywood, it's very entertaining and humorous, but not gripping enough for me.<br><b>Eaten (Scenes from a Moving Picture):</b>3<br>ARGH. I have written on my notepad: 'SEXSEXSEXSEXSEX. GROSSED OUT. NEED SHOWER.'That pretty much summarizes how I feel about this story. ...Bloomin' heteros. <br><b>The White Road:</b>3.5<br>Cool, kind of story you can read over and over again and interpret in many different ways.<br><b>Queen Of Knives:</b>4.5<br>Very alluring; I analysed this to death. I fathomed all sorts of underlying messages and things I could take away. Personally I took this idea of being trapped in a loveless marriage to result in the disappearance. In addition, it's also delectably written. I devoured this story in one bite. <br><b>Changes:</b>4*<br>Exceedingly powerful, especially the end. The mere fact that Rajit (a Scientist) was referring to the people as 'Angels' was of pivotal importance to me. I took away my own meanings for this, some of which I'm certain Gaiman wasn't even attempting to convey. I thought the significance of 'Angels' meant that a conceivably genderless society - or a society in which gender holds no meaning - could be perceived as being that of an angelic, peaceful community. That's just a fraction of what I took away from this, though.<br><b>The Daughter of Owls:</b>2<br>I didn't find this story interesting. The title was inviting but the tale disappointed. I followed everything that happened with little interest as to what <b>would</b> eventually happen.<br><b>Shoggoth's Old Peculiar:</b>2<br>Looking back, I don't even remember this story. Needless to say I wasn't that impressed. Beautifully written (as always, oh Gaiman, you wonderful thing) but with little quality for me to recall. I'll duplicate the comment for above: I didn't find this story interesting. The title was inviting but the tale disappointed. I followed everything that happened with little interest as to what <b>would</b> eventually happen.<br><b>Virus:</b>3<br>Interesting, cryptic, scary. It reminded me of that short film titled <i>Virus</i> too. <br><b>Looking for the Girl:</b>4/4.5<br>This reminded me a lot of <i>Death in Venice</i> and whilst I didn't have the opportunity to picture a beautiful prepubescent boy walking among the streets of Italy, I still engaged with the divine narrative that retained this sense of beauty never being able to be obtained. I'm also reminded of McConaughey's:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385252ra/744118.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Bay Wolf:</b>3<br>I'm always captivated by mythical creatures, so I relished this little anecdote (though I don't remember much about it - probably because I was nodding off). <br><b>Fifteen Painted Cards from a Vampire Tarot:</b>5*<br>A collection within a collection: an array of segmented texts that evoke mystery and awe. I loved the relativity toward Tarot cards in particular, especially 'The Fool'. <br><b>We Can Get Them for You Wholesale:</b>4.5*<br>Hilarious and ambiguously intriguing. <i>'They'd been ready for a long time, but they had to be asked.'</i> It reminded me of Vampires having to be granted permission to cross the threshold into our world. <br><b>One Life, Furnished in Early Moorcock:</b>3<br>All I have written down is: 'Something missing, liked the beginning though.' Very informative, April. <br><b>Cold Colors:</b>2.5<br>All I remember is confusion. <br><b>The Sweeper of Dreams:</b>3.5<br>A magical ideal, one that need not be questioned in the unknown and mystical land of dreams. <br><b>Foreign Parts:</b>3.5<br>Excusing the awkward descriptions of symptoms deriving from venereal disease, the alienation of the lower regions of the protagonists body is open to interpretation. The real interest I had was determining whether this was a tale of possession or dispossession<br><b>Vampire Sestina:</b>5*<br>Sensual and delightful, it certainly appealed to my extreme love of Vampiresque material. Kudos to Gaiman also for succeeding in writing quite possibly the toughest form of verse out there.<br><b>Mouse:</b>2<br>Curious but a tale that scurried away pretty easily from my train of thought. <br><b>The Sea Change:</b>4<br>I love the sea and aquatic life in general, therefore I was pretty gripped with this story. I'm also a sucker for mermaids. <br><b>When We Went To See The End of The World by Dawnie:Morningside, age 11 1/4:</b>4<br>This really disturbed me. I don't know why, it just seemed like the complete representation of evil. It maintained the sense of inventive, fictitious evil whilst holding the innocence and relativity of real life. The most blatant representation of this is the mere use of the narration of an 11-year-old. <br><b>Desert Wind:</b>3<br>Nicely told anecdote; it really brings forth the sensation of regret and longing to be somewhere else (which is the reason I read Gaimans books in the first place). I would like to go with the people too. <br><b>Tastings:</b>4.5*<br>Oh, more sexy times. I actually loved the idea of something so frequently deemed emotionless or meaningless in the promiscuity of modern society becoming a personal necessity to someone's character. To be frank, I pried open this story like some sort of literary autopsy and picked apart meanings and interpretations for hours. <br><b>Babycakes:</b>4*<br><i>'We'll figure something out.'</i> An almost dystopian feel to this, which I always admire. Very haunting and inhuman - yet possible. Foreshadowing the horror of human existence. Superb. <br><b>Murder Mysteries:</b>4<br>I'm not Christian, so forgive me for not fully immersing myself in the retelling of creation or rather Gaiman's 'take' on it. I relished the wholehearted symbolism throughout though. <br><b>Snow, Glass and Apples:</b>3<br>I expected this to be one of my favourites, but sadly it's something that I feel suffered from my high expectations. I originally heard of this in Gaiman's extra in <i>Stardust</i> and thought it was going to be magnificent. It was pretty good, and will forever leave a 'stain' on the Snow White tale for me personally, but truthfully I was expecting more. <br><br>I originally intended to read one story per night, as it seemed pretty easy to do so; all of the stories are fairly unique and eclectic. However, I was far too engaged to pass up the opportunity to finish the book all at once. I even made notes on each tale after finishing them. <br><br>Looking back, it’s quite hard to give an overall summary. It’s a wonderful, disturbing, downright peculiar collection of stories that spins you from one adventure to the next weaved in with Gaiman's imaginary genius. Some were decent, others spectacular, few just okay. I frequently sensed some stories were ones that either needed to be developed more, or ones that didn't have enough promise and shouldn't have made it onto the page.<br><br>Overall rating: <b>3.5.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13587725593892175782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_379644391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379644391" />
    <a title="Petergiaquinta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159895-petergiaquinta"><img alt="Petergiaquinta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304003529p2/4159895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379644391?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petergiaquinta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petergiaquinta" href="/user/show/4159895-petergiaquinta">Petergiaquinta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780380973644" href="/book/show/531127.Smoke_and_Mirrors">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379644391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14685249863921566544">A guilty pleasure, sure, but with Ray Bradbury's death, I'd suggest that Neil Gaiman is the best storyteller we have today.<br/><br/>Consider the words of Harry Bailly (he of the Tabard Inn, not George's brother): "And which of yow that bereth hym best of alle / That is to seyn that telleth in this caas / Tales of best sentence and moost solaas / Shal have a soper at oure aller cost." And I'd buy Gaiman a meal or three for this sundry collection of tales pulled together from over the years and published i</span>
  <span id="freeText14685249863921566544" style="display:none">A guilty pleasure, sure, but with Ray Bradbury's death, I'd suggest that Neil Gaiman is the best storyteller we have today.<br /><br />Consider the words of Harry Bailly (he of the Tabard Inn, not George's brother): "And which of yow that bereth hym best of alle / That is to seyn that telleth in this caas / Tales of best sentence and moost solaas / Shal have a soper at oure aller cost." And I'd buy Gaiman a meal or three for this sundry collection of tales pulled together from over the years and published in <i>Smoke and Mirrors</i>.<br /><br />You might think I'm just showing off with the Middle English, but I don't think it's too much of a stretch to draw parallels between Gaiman and Chaucer. Chaucer's <i>Tales</i> cover a wide range of genres, from the romance to the fabliau to the beast fable to the exemplum and everything in between, and Gaiman uses just as wide a contemporary pallet as Chaucer employed from the Middle Ages. Gaiman moves from the hard-boiled to the horror story; he blends prose and poetry with sci-fi, the sacred and the secular; he has an erotic (?) offering here that transcends mommy porn; heck, he even writes a sestina with vampires in it that works...and that alone has to testify to the genius of the man. Elsewhere Gaiman does everything from the full-blown novel to YA to children's lit; he's written screenplays and comic books, and just about everything he does is golden. Sure he's had some missteps, and not everything in <i>Smoke and Mirrors</i> succeeds at the same level, but hey, the Friar's Tale is a bit dull and the Priest's lengthy sermon is practically unreadable.<br /><br />And like Chaucer (working from Bocaccio and Petrarch and the Thousand and One Nights among other sources), Gaiman is often at his best when he is reworking earlier stories and authors, especially fairy tales and folk tales. His version of Snow White here is a fascinating retelling that's going to stick with me for a long time, and one of my favorites in the book ("Shoggoth's Old Peculiar") grows out of Lovecraft. And even though it's goofy as hell, I even like his pastiche of <i>Beowulf</i> and <i>Baywatch</i> with Larry Talbot thrown in as an added plus.<br /><br />Finally, and thanks for sticking with me this long, Gaiman addresses many of the same concerns Chaucer had: greed and hypocrisy, dreams and where they come from, what makes a good marriage, the role of women in a male-dominated society, and on and on (the intertwining roles of magic and technology in "Cold Colors"? try the Franklin's Tale), but through them all, both authors are really interested in the whole idea of stories and story telling and what makes a good story. And what that is, if you go back to Harry Bailly, is that right blend of "best sentence and moost solaas," and Neil Gaiman just about always gets it right.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14685249863921566544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2293228999" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2293228999" />
    <a title="Lucy Banks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57486568-lucy-banks"><img alt="Lucy Banks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483536933p2/57486568.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2293228999?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Banks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Banks" href="/user/show/57486568-lucy-banks">Lucy Banks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2293228999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14204874826540541310"><b>A little disappointing, though with some flourishes of fabulousness.</b><br/><br/>I'm a <i>huge</i> Neil Gaiman fan. So much so, I cite him as one of the authors that made me want to write. Most of his books are fantastically imaginative, exciting and wonderfully plotted, and a couple of them rank among my all-time favourite books. <br/><br/>As a result, I launched into his collection of short stories with high expectations. I should say, for the record, I like short stories - I apprediate the whole 'bite-sized' concept, that</span>
  <span id="freeText14204874826540541310" style="display:none"><b>A little disappointing, though with some flourishes of fabulousness.</b><br /><br />I'm a <i>huge</i> Neil Gaiman fan. So much so, I cite him as one of the authors that made me want to write. Most of his books are fantastically imaginative, exciting and wonderfully plotted, and a couple of them rank among my all-time favourite books. <br /><br />As a result, I launched into his collection of short stories with high expectations. I should say, for the record, I like short stories - I apprediate the whole 'bite-sized' concept, that you can devour a whole tale in a single setting; it's a bit like having a snack before you settle for a big main meal! However, with this particular collection, a few of the 'snacks' left me a bit unsatisfied. <br /><br />The book gets off to a cracking start with <i>Chivalry</i>, a hilarious story of an old dear who finds the Holy Grail in a charity shop. I was chuckling away throughout the tale, and rubbing my hands with glee, taking it as a sign of things to come. Likewise, I adored <i>Troll Bridge</i>, which cleverly spun the original fairy-tale, taking it in a fresh and surprising direction. <br /><br />However, the book soon became bogged down with a couple of stories that didn't really contribute much (in my opinion). This was particularly the case with the poems; which for me, mostly fell flat. I'm no poem connoisseur, but I do know a good poem when I read one, and I didn't feel that any of these fell into that category. <br /><br />That being said, there were several stories that stuck out as being great. <i>We Can Get Them For You Wholesale</i>, a story about haggling with assassins via the Yellow Pages, is utter brilliance, as is <i>Looking For the Girl</i>; an eerie tale of a man spotting the same woman in countless copies of men's magazines over the years, who never seems to age. Many of the excellent stories could have been filled out and extended into full-length novels, in my opinion. <br /><br />Perhaps if the multiple poems had been stripped out of the book, I would have rated this book a lot higher. Would I give Neil Gaiman's future short stories a try? Yes, definitely. But I think I'd give his poetry a miss! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14204874826540541310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12992525383172014250" style="display:none">This collection of short stories was a bit of a mixed bag for me. I picked it up because well, it’s Gaiman and I can’t say no to his work. I thought there were quite a few good stories that I really enjoyed and even loved but on the whole, most of them were meh. The ones I didn’t enjoy weren’t terrible per say just not my taste and a bit boring in some cases. What I really loved is that there was a lot of variety in this collection, it had so many different kinds of stories and subjects. It really explored it all, from quirky to weird to enchanting and even a little bit of horror. I always appreciate a wide variety of subjects in a short story collection! So while a lot of the stories didn’t work for me, I’m still glad I read it because there were a few really brilliant gems scattered amongst the rocks. </span>

<div id="review_1334818531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1334818531" />
    <a title="Wayne Barrett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21372390-wayne-barrett"><img alt="Wayne Barrett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601067617p2/21372390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1334818531?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wayne Barrett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wayne Barrett" href="/user/show/21372390-wayne-barrett">Wayne Barrett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780380973644" href="/book/show/531127.Smoke_and_Mirrors">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=five-star-favorites">five-star-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=short-story-collection">short-story-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1334818531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2182369374114966775">...Drops of water fell like diamonds from the Angel Lucifer's perfect fingers... From the short story, 'Murder Mysteries'<br/>About half way through this volume of short's I was thinking this would probably be a 4 star, maybe a 3.5 actual. Now that I am at the end, having examined the work as a whole, and considering the power of the last 2 stories, I had to rate this a 5. <br/>I love the way Neil mixed it up. The collection seemed to be a potpourri of short stories, prose, poetry and lyrical verse. I cou</span>
  <span id="freeText2182369374114966775" style="display:none">...Drops of water fell like diamonds from the Angel Lucifer's perfect fingers... From the short story, 'Murder Mysteries'<br />About half way through this volume of short's I was thinking this would probably be a 4 star, maybe a 3.5 actual. Now that I am at the end, having examined the work as a whole, and considering the power of the last 2 stories, I had to rate this a 5. <br />I love the way Neil mixed it up. The collection seemed to be a potpourri of short stories, prose, poetry and lyrical verse. I could feel his love of mythology, a little touch of H.P. Lovecraft, and another side that I think of as a British Chuck Palahniuk.<br />The last 2 stories, 'Murder Mysteries', and 'Snow, Glass, Apples',made this entire book well worth the read. <br />Murder Mysteries was a unique play on the mythology of God, Lucifer and the angels that I found to be particularly entertaining and thought provoking. Very well done. And Snow, Glass, Apples was also a twist on the old story of Snow White. <br />Neil Gaiman has a style and imagination that makes him one of my favorites. And Smoke and Mirrors reflects his story telling gifts brilliantly. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2182369374114966775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5992293810515115366">DNF @71%<br/>This book has been on my TBR for years, so naturally I had very high hopes. To say I am disappointed is a massive understatement... Most stories are boring, sometimes downright bad. Maybe I'm missing something, maybe I'm not. Maybe it's just how old this collection is--I wasn't even born when it was published. (Edit: I was one when it was published.)<br/><br/>That said, I did enjoy <i>Good Omens</i>, so I'm not entirely giving up on Neil Gaiman's work.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>List of Stories:</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>1. The Wedding Present:</b> 2.5 stars</span>
  <span id="freeText5992293810515115366" style="display:none">DNF @71%<br />This book has been on my TBR for years, so naturally I had very high hopes. To say I am disappointed is a massive understatement... Most stories are boring, sometimes downright bad. Maybe I'm missing something, maybe I'm not. Maybe it's just how old this collection is--I wasn't even born when it was published. (Edit: I was one when it was published.)<br /><br />That said, I did enjoy <i>Good Omens</i>, so I'm not entirely giving up on Neil Gaiman's work.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>List of Stories:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>1. The Wedding Present:</b> 2.5 stars. <br />So clever of Neil Gaiman to put this story in the introduction to “trick” those who don’t read introductions. <br />I read this one a while back. I remember it being creepy and having an interesting message about the power of negative thinking. <br /><br /><b>2. Chivalry:</b> 1 star.<br />So I've listened to this story twice now, and it's still not managing to hold my attention. I suppose I'll just move on.<br /><br /><b>3. Nicholas Was...:</b> 1 star.<br />This one, I heard thrice. I guess it's interesting, assuming I understood what it's about. I know it was for a Christmas card and it's exactly 100 words long, which is cool.<br /><br /><b>4. The Price:</b> 1 star.<br />A story about a black cat named "Black Cat". A boring story, and I'm starting to think I'll feel similarly about all the upcoming stories...<br /><br /><b>5. Troll Bridge:</b> 2 stars.<br />This is quite a strange story. It was annoying at first, but I liked the ending.<br /><br /><b>6. Don't Ask Jack:</b> no rating. <br />What was that? I thought the story was still starting, and then it ended too abruptly...<br /><br /><b>7. The Goldfish Pool and Other Stories:</b> 1.5 stars.<br />This was one of the longer stories thus far. While I managed to get a sense of the characters, this story did not have much plot, not to mention there's nothing speculative about it. This story just left me underwhelmed and considering either putting this book down or drastically adjusting my expectations.<br /><br /><b>8. The White Road:</b> 3 stars. <br />This was... strange. It’s written in verse - that aspect is really good and the author’s narration is perfect. The story itself wasn’t great, but not bad. The first truly promising tale in the collection so far. <br /><br /><b>9. Queen of Knives:</b> 3 stars. <br />Not bad, not bad at all. We’re finally getting somewhere! <br /><br /><b>10. Changes:</b> 0.5 stars.<br />...<br /><br /><b>11. The Daughter of Owls:</b> 1 star.<br />Another pointless one...<br /><br /><b>12. Shoggoth's Old Peculiar:</b> 2.5 stars.<br />MC is a Metallurgy student! Interesting story.<br /><br /><b>13. Virus:</b> 3 stars.<br />I love the prose of this one! Has a certain fable-like feel.<br /><br /><b>14. Looking for the Girl:</b> 0.5 stars.<br />DNF.<br /><br /><b>15. Only the End of the World Again:</b> 2.5 stars. <br />Not bad. <br /><br /><b>16. Bay Wolf:</b> 1 star. <br />Hmmm... am I missing something? This could also apply to all the above stories.<br /><br /><b>17. We Can Get Them For You Wholesale:</b> 1 star.<br />Restarted this story at least thrice and still... Quite unmemorable.<br /><br /><b>18. One Life, Furnished in Early Moorcock:</b> no rating.<br />.........<br />DNF<br /><br /><b>19. Cold Colors:</b> no rating.<br />DNF<br /><br /><b>20. The Sweeper of Dreams:</b> 2 stars.<br /><br /><b>21. Foreign Parts:</b> 0.5 stars.<br />This was plain bad.<br /><br /><b>22. Vampire Sestina:</b> 3 stars.<br />This was... it was good, surprisingly. The story is quite short, and every word was well-placed and to the point. <br /><br /><b>23. Mouse:</b><br /><b>24. The Sea Change:</b><br /><b>25. When We Went to See the End of the World by Dawnie Morningside:</b><br /><b>26. Desert Wind:</b><br /><b>27. Tastings:</b><br /><b>28. Babycakes:</b><br /><b>29. Murder Mysteries:</b><br /><b>30. Snow, Glass, Apples:</b> 0.5 stars.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4476681611447644259">My first ever book filled with short stories and, naturally, it was BRILLIANT! I honestly expected Neil Gaiman to deliver a somewhat magical experience since he never disappointed me so far. However, I'm new to short stories and didn't know if it was for me since I usually prefer novels. But this collection has some real gems!<br/>Chilling stories, funny stories, sometimes stories with only a couple of lines, other times quite long short stories, but ALWAYS stories with wit and more than two hidden m</span>
  <span id="freeText4476681611447644259" style="display:none">My first ever book filled with short stories and, naturally, it was BRILLIANT! I honestly expected Neil Gaiman to deliver a somewhat magical experience since he never disappointed me so far. However, I'm new to short stories and didn't know if it was for me since I usually prefer novels. But this collection has some real gems!<br />Chilling stories, funny stories, sometimes stories with only a couple of lines, other times quite long short stories, but ALWAYS stories with wit and more than two hidden messages. There was only one I actually disliked. And, as a bonus, my edition of the book not only had a foreword but also background information on every single one of the stories, which gave a great insight. <br />I will definitely read the next two collections as well.!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4476681611447644259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2690937500" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2690937500" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61529120-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559298134p2/61529120.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2690937500?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/61529120-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2690937500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5123706861962475022">This collection of short stories was the perfect way to introduce me to the works of Neil Gaiman. I loved his style of writing. I was afraid it might be a little pretentious and too high-brow for me, but it was quite the opposite. It was simple, enjoyable and highly imaginative. <br/><br/>I mean, it's pretty obvious that in a book of short stories, one will not love ALL of them, but I really enjoyed more than half of the stories and the only problem I had with the remaining ones were that they went comple</span>
  <span id="freeText5123706861962475022" style="display:none">This collection of short stories was the perfect way to introduce me to the works of Neil Gaiman. I loved his style of writing. I was afraid it might be a little pretentious and too high-brow for me, but it was quite the opposite. It was simple, enjoyable and highly imaginative. <br /><br />I mean, it's pretty obvious that in a book of short stories, one will not love ALL of them, but I really enjoyed more than half of the stories and the only problem I had with the remaining ones were that they went completely over my head. (I'll probably, hopefully, get them after a few more readings.)<br /><br />What amazed me was the sheer variety of themes I got to read. There were stories and poems about cats, vampires, holy grails, fairytale characters, writers, little children, trolls, foxes and so much more. I felt that some stories were just waiting to be made into novels. I don’t know why, but I really want the story ‘Changes’ to be co-written by Neil Gaiman and Stephen King. I would probably be one of the first people to go and buy that book. By the way, ‘Babycakes’ is going to haunt me forever.<br /><br />I really loved how the author sort of gave the background and inspiration behind each story in the introduction (which incidentally, contained an extra short story). It was interesting to follow his crazy train of thought.<br /><br />Note to self: Look up Lisa Snellings’ sculptures.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5123706861962475022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_913465072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/913465072" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/913465072?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061450167" href="/book/show/1358538.Smoke_and_Mirrors">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer913465072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16454808581910262032">SMOKE AND MIRRORS Review, or My Final Review For a While I'm a Neil Gaiman fanboy. I've loved all of his novels and a great deal of his short fiction, but this collection was marred with either lackluster outings or poems I couldn't enjoy because I personally don't understand what makes them poems. The latter is my own fault, and I do not hold it against the author. The former, on the other hand, is all Gaiman's fault. Many of these stories lack purpose, are nothing more than words compiled into</span>
  <span id="freeText16454808581910262032" style="display:none">SMOKE AND MIRRORS Review, or My Final Review For a While I'm a Neil Gaiman fanboy. I've loved all of his novels and a great deal of his short fiction, but this collection was marred with either lackluster outings or poems I couldn't enjoy because I personally don't understand what makes them poems. The latter is my own fault, and I do not hold it against the author. The former, on the other hand, is all Gaiman's fault. Many of these stories lack purpose, are nothing more than words compiled into sentences and paragraphs. I can dig tales that have no definitive ending, or open endings, as it were, but when a piece of fiction has no reason whatsoever I fail to understand how or why it made it to print. Gaiman goes into great detail about how each of the stories in this collection came to be, and I can't help but wonder if the editors who requested a number of these stories only paid for them because they'd asked Gaiman for something and he delivered. Then, said editors felt responsible, perhaps thinking, "Well, we did ask for... something, and he did deliver." The biggest culprit here being the first outing, "Chivalry", wherein nothing happens other than a knight decked out in full armor (in modern times, mind you) trying time and time again to procure the holy grail from a stubborn old woman. In the end, Good Knight Galaad gets his grail and the reader's left wondering exactly what the hell was the story's purpose? There's no conflict, no tension, no drama, no twist, and not even a hint of climax. "Chivalry" accomplished nothing aside from making me slam my forehead into my desk in an attempt to knock the banality of the tale from my conscious mind. I think that, had I read SMOKE AND MIRRORS instead of listening to the audio book, I would have disliked far more of these stories than I did. Gaiman brought a certain whimsical panache to lesser tales, making them a great deal more interesting (e.g. "Troll Bridge", "Shoggoth's Old Peculiar" and "We Can Get Them for You Wholesale"). I think this came from knowing how the author felt the dialogue and prose should be read in order to get the most from the verbiage.<br /> <br />The stories that made me want to stick ice picks in my ears were: "Chivalry", "Don't Ask Jack", "The Daughter of Owls", and "One Life, Furnished in Early Moorcock". I didn't simply dislike these stories, I downright loathed them. Even Gaiman's narration seemed dull, as if he were apologizing for their existence by phoning in his performance. <br /> <br />The tales that stood out are as follows: "The Price", "Troll Bridge", "The Goldfish Pool and Other Stories", "Changes", "Shoggoth's Old Peculiar" (which didn't have a purpose either, but was enjoyable nonetheless because of the odd characters), "Only the End of the World Again". "Bay Wolf", "We can Get Them for You Wholesale", and "Mouse". Basically, half the collection was worth my time. Everything else was either meaningless or downright boring. Still, not a single entry in SMOKE AND MIRRORS matched the brilliance of his novels. I was hoping for short stroies on par with CORALINE or THE OCEAN AT THE END OF THE LANE or AMERICAN GODS. Sadly, I was disappointed. <br /> <br />All other stories not mentioned above were wholly unmentionable or entirely forgettable. Meaning, I couldn't even be bothered to complain about them.<br /> <br />In summation: If you're looking for a collection packed with amazing short stories, you can do far better than this. SMOKE AND MIRRORS is not the worst short story collection I've read, but it comes close. When Gaiman is on, he's terrific and magical and wonderfully creative, but when he's bad, sweet baby Tom Cruise, he'll make you want to castrate him with a rusty battleaxe then boil the dismembered bits in a vat of acid. Still, this grouping of fiction is well written. Even the worst of these tales are readable, which cannot be said for every short story author. Instead of this, I recommend ANANSI BOYS, THE GRAVEYARD BOOK, AMERICAN GODS, CORALINE (and, no, it's not only a children's book), THE OCEAN AT THE END OF THE LANE, or any of Gaiman's other novels. I highly recommend his series of SANDMAN comics, if you can get your hands on them, that is. If you would like a better collection from a different author, try BOOKS OF BLOOD, by Clive Barker (in my opinion, Barker is much better at short fiction than he'll ever be as a novelist), SKELETON CREW, by Stephen King, and any collection by Ray Bradbury.<br /> <br />2.5 out of 5 severely disappointed stars. (If you're reading this on Goodreads, I've rounded up to three.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16454808581910262032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Latharia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/140880-latharia"><img alt="Latharia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1182310614p2/140880.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34782355?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Latharia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Latharia" href="/user/show/140880-latharia">Latharia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060934705" href="/book/show/1116806.Smoke_and_Mirrors">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34782355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7042112666557437597">Wow. I have to say that just about every story in this collection was highly engaging, and I had strong emotional reactions to several of them, and many "gotcha" type moments. Gaiman is, indeed, a master storyteller. Some of my favorite bits, without giving too much away for those of you who need to add this to your "to read" stack: <br/><br/>- the sad workings of Peter's mind in "We Can Get Them For You Wholesale"<br/>- the explanation of those who've spurned "The Sweeper of Dreams"<br/>- the evolution of perceive</span>
  <span id="freeText7042112666557437597" style="display:none">Wow. I have to say that just about every story in this collection was highly engaging, and I had strong emotional reactions to several of them, and many "gotcha" type moments. Gaiman is, indeed, a master storyteller. Some of my favorite bits, without giving too much away for those of you who need to add this to your "to read" stack: <br /><br />- the sad workings of Peter's mind in "We Can Get Them For You Wholesale"<br />- the explanation of those who've spurned "The Sweeper of Dreams"<br />- the evolution of perceived morality in "Changes"<br />- the mundane conversational aspects of "Tastings"<br />- the story embedded within the story of "Murder Mysteries"<br /><br />I would like to say that this is a wonderful book to have on one's nightstand, to read a short story before bedtime, but I can't say that. Many of the stories (Don't Ask Jack, The White Road, and Snow,Glass,Apples in particular) were downright emotionally disturbing. Good, but disturbing. Don't Ask Jack actually generated a nightmare! *shudder* Great job, Gaiman. *wink*</span>
  <a data-text-id="7042112666557437597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/806279811?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" href="/user/show/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh">Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤</a>

<div id="review_1840975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1840975" />
    <a title="J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/123082-j"><img alt="J" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1840975?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J" href="/user/show/123082-j">J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Vampires</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1840975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer523173616274571805">A note: I expect more than I should from this author. I find him to be a brilliant idea man with little substance.<br/><br/>-Suggested Reading Order:<br/><br/>Murder Mystery<br/>Tastings<br/>Snow, Glass, Apples <br/>Only the End of the World Again<br/>Shoggoth’s Old Peculiar <br/>We Can Get Them for You Wholesale<br/>Chivalry<br/>Cold Colors<br/>The Price<br/><br/>Chivalry- an old woman buys the Holy Grail. A full-armored knight comes to seek the Grail. Cute, long-run and dry. The most wonderful thing about this story is that it is quaint and written as gabbish; a</span>
  <span id="freeText523173616274571805" style="display:none">A note: I expect more than I should from this author. I find him to be a brilliant idea man with little substance.<br /><br />-Suggested Reading Order:<br /><br />Murder Mystery<br />Tastings<br />Snow, Glass, Apples <br />Only the End of the World Again<br />Shoggoth’s Old Peculiar <br />We Can Get Them for You Wholesale<br />Chivalry<br />Cold Colors<br />The Price<br /><br />Chivalry- an old woman buys the Holy Grail. A full-armored knight comes to seek the Grail. Cute, long-run and dry. The most wonderful thing about this story is that it is quaint and written as gabbish; a runabout talkative form of day-to-day meandering, paying no heed to the extraordinary.<br /><br />Nicholas Was… - my favorite line "Once every year they forced him, sobbing and protesting, into Endless Night." This is a short short story. It seems, in this piece, there was more to be said but wasn’t.<br /><br />The Price- The beginning of this piece is bloody brilliant, reflecting harlequin mythos. The story sidesteps this flight of fancy to anecdote, betraying itself with its narrative<br /><br />Troll Bridge- The strength is the child’s voice (which continues and becomes outlived). The narrative stretches into the mundane: a point and picture of nothingness, an ode to the anticlimactic where, at the end, the story snuffs itself out of hopelessness… like a suicidal cigarette. <br /><br />The White Road- These story-poems were glanced over with some volume of interest. The White Road- could’ve been the premise for the Corpse Bride, except that at the scene where the corpse bride was supposed to get killed, she does not and lives thereafter. <br /><br />Changes- A summary of a man and his time split from an invention- a (not the) cure for cancer, side effect- sex change, and what becomes of it as seen by him. <br /><br />The Daughters of Owls- Phun with mysspellinks. <br /><br />Shoggoth’s Old Peculiar- Gaiman pays homage to H.P. Lovecraft, typing his lines and taking his name. The descriptive presence shows Gaiman's strength as the main character muddles about a town conversing with two drunkards spouting Lovecraft at lengths with lists of that and this. <br /><br />Looking for the Girl- The main character buys a dirty magazine in his youth and immortalizes the girl spread between the pages. He devotes his life to finding her, becoming a photographer, selling off all of his worldly possessions, and buying all of the magazines (of which she appears at different intervals in his life- the same and in age, but with a different name). <br /><br />Only the End of the World Again- Read this substanceless story for its language (it has a Scooby-Doo-ish plot).<br /><br />Bay Wolf- Fighting something from the Deep! Narrated in pulp “and then I ripped his arm off” fashion. <br /><br />We Can Get Them For You Wholesale- Brilliant first 3 pages! A man searches through a phone book for an assassin to kill the man who’s cheating with his girlfriend. <br /><br />Cold Colors- Crazy cool Dealing with computers and computer lingo, software, hardware mixed between metaphors. My favorite part was pigeon selling- people would buy them and spread their blood around their computer.<br /><br />The Sweeper of Dreams- T’was a nice short; think the ending was a “I have to end this and… meh.”<br /><br />Vampire Sestina- A vampire poem. The word blood is used. Ironically, the word suck is not.<br /><br />Mouse- What’s happening takes place in one paragraph near the end of the story. Everything else is exposition to that idea.<br /><br />Tastings- It’s sexually explitious! An erotic tale with a twist into supernatural fiction. Very well written.<br /><br />Babycakes- A story about eating babies… (sweet)<br /><br />Murder Mysteries- I waded through 292 pages to read this story!<br /><br />Snow, Glass, Apples- …I like the idea of holding her heart on the wall above the bed. <br /><br />(The short stories not mentioned are partiularly: MEH!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="523173616274571805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3796845393593796590" style="display:none">I was reading reviews about this one and at some point, I realized that I read about half of it a couple of years ago. I DNF'd because I was bored out of my mind, so it's not surprising that I completely forgot about it. There were a couple of stories that I liked (<i>We Can Get Them For You Wholesale</i> is one that comes to mind) but all in all, I wasn't impressed. <br /><br />I'm still trying to figure out what it is about Gaiman that makes him so loved by almost everyone. I usually like his ideas but hate the execution. I will never understand why <i>American Gods</i> has a rating of 4.11. <i>Never</i>.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780755322831" href="/book/show/597623.Smoke_and_Mirrors">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2649150615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14254132309335629023">Undoubtedly Mr Gaiman is greatly talented but I didn't really enjoy all of these tales. That's the problem with short stories; you just start to get into them and then they're finished.<br/><br/>Definitely worth a read but no more than 3 out of 5 stars for me. </span>

          </span>
        </div>
